  52. As stated by other reviewers, this isn't 100% Hyalutronic acid. It contains 3 ingredients total. One of them is Benzylalcohol. There are two types of alcohols &#34;fatty&#34; alcohols which will hold moisture in the skin, and Solvent alcohols which will breakdown moisture. Usually you want nothing to do with a solvent alcohol in your skin care product as it breaks down the skin's nature moisture barrier and can cause damage. Benzylalcohol is a solvent alcohol.<br /><br />Because of that, this product actually was the opposite of moisturizing for me. I would have preferred something without an alcohol and instead a preservative.<br /><br />The product isn't bad necessarily and the price point makes it incredibly affordable. Your experience may differ.

  165. I purchased this as a replacement for another bottle of 100% pure Hyaluronic Acid I usually buy from a spa in California. I was hoping to save some money and decided to try this one. Well, I didn't save any money since I won't be using this bottle by Timeless Skincare. There are 3 ingredients and the second one on the list is Benzyl Alcohol. It's used as a preservative in cosmetics but is one of the alcohols you should avoid if you have sensitive skin. Well I do and I know there are a lot of people out there who do as well. If you are prone to break outs from certain products, look at the ingredient lists and you will find one of the alcohols as an irritant (ethyl alcohol -- also known as denatured, or SD, alcohol and ethanol -- benzyl alcohol, methyl and isopropyl alcohol).<br /><br />I also noticed a difference in how quickly this product seemed to disappear on the skin. I tested it on my hands and compared it w/ the other brand I normally use. The Timeless HLA evaporated much more quickly than my previous HLA. While it slightly improved moisture on my hand, it did not compare to the moisture level from my original HLA. I also tested it out on my face at night. I have dry skin in colder weather and need extra moisture. I topped this w/ a heavy night cream. The next morning, I found a few red itchy spots on my face and my skin felt dryer. The itchiness lasted the whole day and was only helped by extra moisturizing during the day w/ coconut oil. I avoided the use of this HLA product ever since and will not be using it again.<br /><br />SO bottom line, use only if you do NOT have sensitive skin. If you do, you risk the chance of irritation. It offers slight moisture but can also dry out the skin after prolonged use due to the benzyl alcohol.

Here is something I found online at: [...]in a article discussing why your skin needs Hyaluronic acid.<br /><br />Hyaluronic acid plays a key role in the skin's extracellular matrix and has been shown to maintain hydration, improve elasticity and protect against free radical damage. In the skin, hyaluronic acid is responsible for capturing water, in turn maintaining the smoothness and plumpness of the skin. When hyaluronic acid is depleted, skin can become dehydrated and lose elasticity, which accentuates lines and furrows.<br /><br />When you use skin care products containing hyaluronic acid, it works by absorbing available moisture from the environment and water already present in the skin. Hyaluronic acid helps the skin retain this moisture, and has a temporary plumping effect on fine lines and wrinkles as the molecules swell. But hyaluronic acid is a costly ingredient, which is why it's important to choose a product with an effective concentration. As a general rule of thumb, the higher up on the ingredient list the hyaluronic acid (or sodium hyaluronate) is, the more potent the product, which means better results for your skin.<br /><br />I have only purchased the Hyaluronic Acid Serum 100% Pure from Timeless.
